</p><p>When Kahlo was six years old, she contracted <a href="/wiki/Polio" title="Polio">polio</a>, which eventually made her right leg grow shorter and thinner than the left.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHerrera200210–20Ankori201344_150-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHerrera200210–20Ankori201344-150">[149]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-153"><a href="#cite_note-153">[b]</a></sup> The illness forced her to be isolated from her peers for months, and she was bullied.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHerrera200210–20Ankori201344–47_154-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHerrera200210–20Ankori201344–47-154">[152]</a></sup> While the experience made her reclusive,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAnkori200218_146-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAnkori200218-146">[145]</a></sup> it made her Guillermo's favorite due to their shared experience of living with disability.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBurrus200813–15Herrera200210–21_155-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBurrus200813–15Herrera200210–21-155">[153]</a></sup> Kahlo credited him for making her childhood "marvelous ... he was an immense example to me of tenderness, of work (photographer and also painter), and above all in understanding for all my problems." He taught her about literature, nature, and philosophy, and encouraged her to play sports to regain her strength, despite the fact that most physical exercise was seen as unsuitable for girls.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHerrera200210–20Burrus2005199Ankori201345Burrus200816_156-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHerrera200210–20Burrus2005199Ankori201345Burrus200816-156">[154]</a></sup> He also taught her photography, and she began to help him retouch, develop, and color photographs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHerrera200210–20Burrus2005199Zamora199018_157-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHerrera200210–20Burrus2005199Zamora199018-157">[155]</a></sup>
</p><p>Due to polio, Kahlo began school later than her peers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEZamora199018_158-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEZamora199018-158">[156]</a></sup> Along with her younger sister Cristina, she attended the local kindergarten and primary school in Coyoacán and was homeschooled for the fifth and sixth grades.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAnkori201358_159-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAnkori201358-159">[157]</a></sup> While Cristina followed their sisters into a convent school, Kahlo was enrolled in a German school due to their father's wishes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAnkori200219_160-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAnkori200219-160">[158]</a></sup> She was soon expelled for disobedience and was sent to a vocational teachers school.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAnkori201358_159-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAnkori201358-159">[157]</a></sup> Her stay at the school was brief, as she was sexually abused by a female teacher.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAnkori201358_159-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAnkori201358-159">[157]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1922, Kahlo was accepted to the elite <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Escuela_Nacional_Preparatoria_(Mexico)" title="Escuela Nacional Preparatoria (Mexico)">National Preparatory School</a>, where she focused on natural sciences with the aim of becoming a physician.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKettenmann200311Herrera200222–27Ankori200219_161-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKettenmann200311Herrera200222–27Ankori200219-161">[159]</a></sup> The institution had only recently begun admitting women, with only 35 girls out of 2,000 students.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKettenmann200311Herrera200222–27_162-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKettenmann200311Herrera200222–27-162">[160]</a></sup> She performed well academically,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHerrera200226–40_10-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHerrera200226–40-10">[10]</a></sup> was a voracious reader, and became "deeply immersed and seriously committed to Mexican culture, political activism and issues of social justice".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAnkori201360–62_163-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAnkori201360–62-163">[161]</a></sup> The school promoted <i><a href="/wiki/Indigenismo_in_Mexico" title="Indigenismo in Mexico">indigenismo</a></i>, a new sense of Mexican identity that took pride in the country's indigenous heritage and sought to rid itself of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Colonial_mindset" title="Colonial mindset">colonial mindset</a> of Europe as superior to Mexico.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAnderson2009120_164-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAnderson2009120-164">[162]</a></sup> Particularly influential to Kahlo at this time were nine of her schoolmates, with whom she formed an informal group called the "Cachuchas" – many of them would become leading figures of the Mexican intellectual elite.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHerrera200226–40Barson200559Burrus2005199Ankori200219_165-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHerrera200226–40Barson200559Burrus2005199Ankori200219-165">[163]</a></sup> They were rebellious and against everything conservative and pulled pranks, staged plays, and debated philosophy and Russian classics.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHerrera200226–40Barson200559Burrus2005199Ankori200219_165-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHerrera200226–40Barson200559Burrus2005199Ankori200219-165">[163]</a></sup> To mask the fact that she was older and to declare herself a "daughter of the revolution", she began saying that she had been born on 7 July 1910, the year the <a href="/wiki/Mexican_Revolution" title="Mexican Revolution">Mexican Revolution</a> began, which she continued throughout her life.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHerrera20025Dexter200513Zamora199019–20_166-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHerrera20025Dexter200513Zamora199019–20-166">[164]</a></sup> She fell in love with Alejandro Gomez Arias, the leader of the group and her first love. Her parents did not approve of the relationship. Arias and Kahlo were often separated from each other, due to the political instability and violence of the period, so they exchanged passionate love letters.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:1_12-3"><a href="#cite_note-:1-12">[12]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:2_167-0"><a href="#cite_note-:2-167">[165]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="1925.E2.80.931930:_Bus_accident_and_marriage_to_Diego_Rivera"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1925–1930:_Bus_accident_and_marriage_to_Diego_Rivera">1925–1930: Bus accident and marriage to Diego Rivera</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Frida_Kahlo,_by_Guillermo_Kahlo_2.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="857" data-file-width="600" decoding="async" height="243" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Frida_Kahlo%2C_by_Guillermo_Kahlo_2.jpg/170px-Frida_Kahlo%2C_by_Guillermo_Kahlo_2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Frida_Kahlo%2C_by_Guillermo_Kahlo_2.jpg/255px-Frida_Kahlo%2C_by_Guillermo_Kahlo_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Frida_Kahlo%2C_by_Guillermo_Kahlo_2.jpg/340px-Frida_Kahlo%2C_by_Guillermo_Kahlo_2.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Frida_Kahlo,_by_Guillermo_Kahlo_2.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Kahlo photographed by her father in 1926</div></div></div><p>On 17 September 1925, Kahlo and her boyfriend, Arias, were on their way home from school. They boarded one bus, but they got off the bus to look for an umbrella that Kahlo had left behind. They then boarded a second bus, which was crowded, and they sat in the back. The driver attempted to pass an oncoming electric <a href="/wiki/Tram" title="Tram">streetcar</a>. The streetcar crashed into the side of the wooden bus, dragging it a few feet. Several passengers were killed in the accident. While Arias suffered minor injuries, Frida was impaled with an iron handrail that went through her pelvis. She later described the injury as "the way a sword pierces a bull". The handrail was removed by Arias and others, which was incredibly painful for Kahlo.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:2_167-1"><a href="#cite_note-:2-167">[165]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKettenmann200317–18_168-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKettenmann200317–18-168">[166]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHerrera200257–60Burrus2005201Ankori200220–21_169-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHerrera200257–60Burrus2005201Ankori200220–21-169">[167]</a></sup>
</p><p>Kahlo suffered many injuries: her <a href="/wiki/Hip_bone" title="Hip bone">pelvic bone</a> had been fractured, her <a href="/wiki/Abdomen" title="Abdomen">abdomen</a> and <a href="/wiki/Uterus" title="Uterus">uterus</a> had been punctured by the rail, her <a href="/wiki/Vertebral_column" title="Vertebral column">spine</a> was broken in three places, her right leg was broken in eleven places, her right foot was crushed and dislocated, her <a href="/wiki/Clavicle" title="Clavicle">collarbone</a> was broken, and her shoulder was dislocated.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:2_167-2"><a href="#cite_note-:2-167">[165]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-170"><a href="#cite_note-170">[168]</a></sup> She spent a month in hospital and two months recovering at home before being able to return to work.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKettenmann200317–18_168-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKettenmann200317–18-168">[166]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHerrera200257–60Burrus2005201Ankori200220–21_169-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHerrera200257–60Burrus2005201Ankori200220–21-169">[167]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-171"><a href="#cite_note-171">[169]</a></sup> As she continued to experience fatigue and back pain, her doctors ordered X-rays, which revealed that the accident had also displaced three <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vertebrae" title="Vertebrae">vertebrae</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKettenmann200317–18Herrera200262–63_172-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKettenmann200317–18Herrera200262–63-172">[170]</a></sup> As treatment she had to wear a plaster corset which confined her to bed rest for the better part of three months.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKettenmann200317–18Herrera200262–63_172-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKettenmann200317–18Herrera200262–63-172">[170]</a></sup>
</p><p>The accident ended Kahlo's dreams of becoming a physician and caused her pain and illness for the rest of her life; her friend <a href="/wiki/Andr%C3%A9s_Henestrosa" title="Andrés Henestrosa">Andrés Henestrosa</a> stated that Kahlo "lived dying".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAnkori2002101Ankori201351_173-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAnkori2002101Ankori201351-173">[171]</a></sup> Kahlo's bed rest was over by late 1927, and she began socializing with her old schoolfriends, who were now at university and involved in student politics. She joined the <a href="/wiki/Mexican_Communist_Party" title="Mexican Communist Party">Mexican Communist Party</a> (PCM) and was introduced to a circle of political activists and artists, including the exiled Cuban communist <a href="/wiki/Julio_Antonio_Mella" title="Julio Antonio Mella">Julio Antonio Mella</a> and the Italian-American photographer <a href="/wiki/Tina_Modotti" title="Tina Modotti">Tina Modotti</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKettenmann200320–22Herrera200278–81Burrus2005201Zamora199031_174-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKettenmann200320–22Herrera200278–81Burrus2005201Zamora199031-174">[172]</a></sup>
</p><p>At one of Modotti's parties in June 1928, Kahlo was introduced to <a href="/wiki/Diego_Rivera" title="Diego Rivera">Diego Rivera</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarnham1998220Zamora199033–34Ankori200220,_139_175-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarnham1998220Zamora199033–34Ankori200220,_139-175">[173]</a></sup> They had met briefly in 1922 when he was painting a mural at her school.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarnham1998220Zamora199033–34Ankori200220_176-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarnham1998220Zamora199033–34Ankori200220-176">[174]</a></sup> Shortly after their introduction in 1928, Kahlo asked him to judge whether her paintings showed enough talent for her to pursue a career as an artist.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEZamora199033–35Burrus2005201Ankori200220_177-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEZamora199033–35Burrus2005201Ankori200220-177">[175]</a></sup> Rivera recalled being impressed by her works, stating that they showed "an unusual energy of expression, precise delineation of character, and true severity ... They had a fundamental plastic honesty, and an artistic personality of their own ... It was obvious to me that this girl was an authentic artist".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHerrera200286–87_178-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHerrera200286–87-178">[176]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Frida_Kahlo_Diego_Rivera_1932.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="407" data-file-width="314" decoding="async" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Frida_Kahlo_Diego_Rivera_1932.jpg/170px-Frida_Kahlo_Diego_Rivera_1932.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Frida_Kahlo_Diego_Rivera_1932.jpg/255px-Frida_Kahlo_Diego_Rivera_1932.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/3/3a/Frida_Kahlo_Diego_Rivera_1932.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Frida_Kahlo_Diego_Rivera_1932.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Kahlo with husband <a href="/wiki/Diego_Rivera" title="Diego Rivera">Diego Rivera</a> in 1932</div></div></div>
<p>Kahlo soon began a relationship with Rivera, who was 20 years her senior and had two common-law wives.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHerrera200279–80,_87–93Ankori200220–21Zamora199037_179-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHerrera200279–80,_87–93Ankori200220–21Zamora199037-179">[177]</a></sup> Kahlo and Rivera were married in a civil ceremony at the town hall of Coyoacán on 21 August 1929.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEZamora199035_180-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEZamora199035-180">[178]</a></sup> Her mother opposed the marriage, and both parents referred to it as a "marriage between an elephant and a dove", referring to the couple's differences in size; Rivera was tall and overweight while Kahlo was petite and fragile.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHerrera200293–100Ankori70–732013_181-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHerrera200293–100Ankori70–732013-181">[179]</a></sup> Regardless, her father approved of Rivera, who was wealthy and therefore able to support Kahlo, who could not work and had to receive expensive medical treatment.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHerrera200293–100_182-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHerrera200293–100-182">[180]</a></sup> The wedding was reported by the Mexican and international press,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEZamora199040Herrera2002Preface_xi_183-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEZamora199040Herrera2002Preface_xi-183">[181]</a></sup> and the marriage was subject to constant media attention in Mexico in the following years, with articles referring to the couple as simply "Diego and Frida".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHerrera2002Preface_xi_184-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHerrera2002Preface_xi-184">[182]</a></sup>
</p><p>Soon after the marriage, in late 1929, Kahlo and Rivera moved to <a href="/wiki/Cuernavaca" title="Cuernavaca">Cuernavaca</a> in the rural state of <a href="/wiki/Morelos" title="Morelos">Morelos</a>, where he had been commissioned to paint murals for the <a href="/wiki/Palace_of_Cort%C3%A9s,_Cuernavaca" title="Palace of Cortés, Cuernavaca">Palace of Cortés</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEZamora199042Herrera2002101–105Burrus2005201_185-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEZamora199042Herrera2002101–105Burrus2005201-185">[183]</a></sup> Around the same time, she resigned her membership of the PCM in support of Rivera, who had been expelled shortly before the marriage for his support of the leftist opposition movement within the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Third_International" title="Third International">Third International</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBurrus2005201Herrera2002101–105Tibol2005191_for_time_for_Rivera's_expulsion_186-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBurrus2005201Herrera2002101–105Tibol2005191_for_time_for_Rivera's_expulsion-186">[184]</a></sup>
</p><p>During the civil war Morelos had seen some of the heaviest fighting, and life in the Spanish-style city of Cuernavaca sharpened Kahlo's sense of a Mexican identity and history.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEUdall200311_19-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUdall200311-19">[19]</a></sup> Similar to many other Mexican women artists and intellectuals at the time,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKettenmann200326–27Albers1999223BlockHoffman-Jeep1998–19998–10Ankori2002144_187-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKettenmann200326–27Albers1999223BlockHoffman-Jeep1998–19998–10Ankori2002144-187">[185]</a></sup> Kahlo began wearing traditional indigenous Mexican peasant clothing to emphasize her <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mestiza" title="Mestiza">mestiza</a></i> ancestry: long and colorful skirts, <i><a href="/wiki/Huipil" title="Huipil">huipils</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Rebozo" title="Rebozo">rebozos</a></i>, elaborate headdresses and masses of jewelry.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHerrera2002109–113Zamora199078–80_188-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHerrera2002109–113Zamora199078–80-188">[186]</a></sup> She especially favored the dress of women from the allegedly <a href="/wiki/Matriarchy" title="Matriarchy">matriarchal</a> society of the <a href="/wiki/Isthmus_of_Tehuantepec" title="Isthmus of Tehuantepec">Isthmus of Tehuantepec</a>, who had come to represent "an authentic and indigenous Mexican cultural heritage" in post-revolutionary Mexico.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHerrera2002101–113Marnham1998228BlockHoffman-Jeep1998–19998–10Dexter200512–13Baddeley199112–13_189-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHerrera2002101–113Marnham1998228BlockHoffman-Jeep1998–19998–10Dexter200512–13Baddeley199112–13-189">[187]</a></sup> The Tehuana outfit allowed Kahlo to express her feminist and anti-colonialist ideals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBaddeley199113–14_190-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBaddeley199113–14-190">[188]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="1931.E2.80.931933:_Travels_in_the_United_States"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1931–1933:_Travels_in_the_United_States">1931–1933: Travels in the United States</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Frida_Kahlo,_by_Guillermo_Kahlo_3.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="666" data-file-width="500" decoding="async" height="226" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Frida_Kahlo%2C_by_Guillermo_Kahlo_3.jpg/170px-Frida_Kahlo%2C_by_Guillermo_Kahlo_3.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Frida_Kahlo%2C_by_Guillermo_Kahlo_3.jpg/255px-Frida_Kahlo%2C_by_Guillermo_Kahlo_3.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Frida_Kahlo%2C_by_Guillermo_Kahlo_3.jpg/340px-Frida_Kahlo%2C_by_Guillermo_Kahlo_3.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Frida_Kahlo,_by_Guillermo_Kahlo_3.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Frida photographed in 1932 by her father, <a href="/wiki/Guillermo_Kahlo" title="Guillermo Kahlo">Guillermo</a></div></div></div>
<p>After Rivera had completed the commission in Cuernavaca in late 1930, he and Kahlo moved to <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco" title="San Francisco">San Francisco</a>, where he painted murals for the Luncheon Club of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/San_Francisco_Stock_Exchange" title="San Francisco Stock Exchange">San Francisco Stock Exchange</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/California_School_of_Fine_Arts" title="California School of Fine Arts">California School of Fine Arts</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHerrera2002114–116Kettenmann200331Marnham231–232_191-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHerrera2002114–116Kettenmann200331Marnham231–232-191">[189]</a></sup> The couple was "feted, lionized, [and] spoiled" by influential collectors and clients during their stay in the city.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHerrera2002117–125Zamora199042–43BlockHoffman-Jeep1998–19998_23-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHerrera2002117–125Zamora199042–43BlockHoffman-Jeep1998–19998-23">[23]</a></sup> Her long love affair with Hungarian-American photographer <a href="/wiki/Nickolas_Muray" title="Nickolas Muray">Nickolas Muray</a> most likely began around this time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPanzer200440–41,_mentions_1931_letter_from_Kahlo_to_Muray,_but_not_entirely_sure_if_this_was_the_beginning_of_affairMarnham1998234–235,_interprets_letter_as_evidence_of_the_beginning_of_affair_192-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPanzer200440–41,_mentions_1931_letter_from_Kahlo_to_Muray,_but_not_entirely_sure_if_this_was_the_beginning_of_affairMarnham1998234–235,_interprets_letter_as_evidence_of_the_beginning_of_affair-192">[190]</a></sup>
</p><p>Kahlo and Rivera returned to Mexico for the summer of 1931, and in the fall traveled to <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a> for the opening of Rivera's retrospective at the <a href="/wiki/Museum_of_Modern_Art" title="Museum of Modern Art">Museum of Modern Art</a> (MoMA). In April 1932, they headed to <a href="/wiki/Detroit" title="Detroit">Detroit</a>, where Rivera had been commissioned to paint murals for the <a href="/wiki/Detroit_Institute_of_Arts" title="Detroit Institute of Arts">Detroit Institute of Arts</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHerrera2002125–130Zamora199043_193-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHerrera2002125–130Zamora199043-193">[191]</a></sup> By this time, Kahlo had become bolder in her interactions with the press, impressing journalists with her fluency in English and stating on her arrival to the city that she was the greater artist of the two of them.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHerrera2002133–160_194-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHerrera2002133–160-194">[192]</a></sup>
</p>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r996844942" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>"Of course he [Rivera] does well for a little boy, but it is I who am the big artist"</p><div class="templatequotecite">— <cite>Frida Kahlo in interview with the <i>Detroit News</i>, 2 February 1933.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-195"><a href="#cite_note-195">[193]</a></sup></cite></div></blockquote>
<p>The year spent in Detroit was a difficult time for Kahlo. Although she had enjoyed visiting San Francisco and New York City, she disliked aspects of American society, which she regarded as colonialist, as well as most Americans, whom she found "boring".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHerrera2002117–125Zamora199042–43Burrus2005202–203Kettenmann200336_for_quote_196-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHerrera2002117–125Zamora199042–43Burrus2005202–203Kettenmann200336_for_quote-196">[194]</a></sup> She disliked having to socialize with capitalists such as <a href="/wiki/Henry_Ford" title="Henry Ford">Henry</a> and <a href="/wiki/Edsel_Ford" title="Edsel Ford">Edsel Ford</a>, and was angered that many of the hotels in Detroit refused to accept Jewish guests.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBurrus2005202Herrera2002133–160_197-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBurrus2005202Herrera2002133–160-197">[195]</a></sup> In a letter to a friend, she wrote that "although I am very interested in all the industrial and mechanical development of the United States", she felt "a bit of a rage against all the rich guys here, since I have seen thousands of people in the most terrible misery without anything to eat and with no place to sleep, that is what has most impressed me here, it is terrifying to see the rich having parties day and night whiles thousands and thousands of people are dying of hunger."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKettenmann200336_for_quote_33-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKettenmann200336_for_quote-33">[33]</a></sup> Kahlo's time in Detroit was also complicated by a pregnancy. Her doctor agreed to perform an abortion, but the medication used was ineffective.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAnkori201387–94_198-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAnkori201387–94-198">[196]</a></sup> Kahlo was deeply ambivalent about having a child and had already undergone an abortion earlier in her marriage to Rivera.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAnkori201387–94_198-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAnkori201387–94-198">[196]</a></sup> Following the failed abortion, she reluctantly agreed to continue with the pregnancy, but miscarried in July, which caused a serious <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hemorrhage" title="Hemorrhage">hemorrhage</a> that required her being hospitalized for two weeks.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHerrera2002133–160Burrus2005201Zamora199046Kettenmann200332Ankori201387–94_32-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHerrera2002133–160Burrus2005201Zamora199046Kettenmann200332Ankori201387–94-32">[32]</a></sup> Less than three months later, her mother died from complications of surgery in Mexico.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHerrera2002133–160Zamora199046_199-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHerrera2002133–160Zamora199046-199">[197]</a></sup>
</p>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1066479718" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><table class="infobox" style="float: right; clear: right; margin:0 0 1.5em 1.5em"><tbody><tr><th States</i> (1932)</a></td></tr><tr><td class="infobox-full-data" colspan="2" style="text-align: left"><img alt="image icon" data-file-height="512" data-file-width="512" decoding="async" height="16" width="16"/> <a class="external text" href="https://www.wikiart.org/en/frida-kahlo/my-birth-1932" rel="nofollow"><i>My Birth</i> (1932)</a></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>Kahlo and Rivera returned to New York in March 1933, for he had been commissioned to paint a mural for the <a href="/wiki/Rockefeller_Center" title="Rockefeller Center">Rockefeller Center</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHerrera2002161–178_200-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHerrera2002161–178-200">[198]</a></sup> During this time, she only worked on one painting, <i>My Dress Hangs There</i> (1934).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHerrera2002161–178_200-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHerrera2002161–178-200">[198]</a></sup> She also gave further interviews to the American press.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHerrera2002161–178_200-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHerrera2002161–178-200">[198]</a></sup> In May, Rivera was fired from the Rockefeller Center project and was instead hired to paint a mural for the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_Workers_School" title="New Workers School">New Workers School</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEZamora199046Herrera2002161–178Kettenmann200338_201-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEZamora199046Herrera2002161–178Kettenmann200338-201">[199]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHerrera2002161–178_200-3"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHerrera2002161–178-200">[198]</a></sup> Although Rivera wished to continue their stay in the United States, Kahlo was homesick, and they returned to Mexico soon after the mural's unveiling in December 1933.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKettenmann200338Herrera2002161–178_202-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKettenmann200338Herrera2002161–178-202">[200]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="1934.E2.80.931949:_La_Casa_Azul_and_declining_health"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1934–1949:_La_Casa_Azul_and_declining_health">1934–1949: La Casa Azul and declining health</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Casa_Habitaci%C3%B3n_Rivera_y_Kalho.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2248" data-file-width="3437" decoding="async" height="144" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Casa_Habitaci%C3%B3n_Rivera_y_Kalho.JPG/220px-Casa_Habitaci%C3%B3n_Rivera_y_Kalho.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Casa_Habitaci%C3%B3n_Rivera_y_Kalho.JPG/330px-Casa_Habitaci%C3%B3n_Rivera_y_Kalho.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Casa_Habitaci%C3%B3n_Rivera_y_Kalho.JPG/440px-Casa_Habitaci%C3%B3n_Rivera_y_Kalho.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Casa_Habitaci%C3%B3n_Rivera_y_Kalho.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Kahlo and Rivera's houses in <a href="/wiki/San_%C3%81ngel" title="San Ángel">San Ángel</a>; they lived there from 1934 until their divorce in 1939, after which it became his studio</div></div></div>
<p>Back in Mexico City, Kahlo and Rivera moved into a new house in the wealthy neighborhood of <a href="/wiki/San_%C3%81ngel" title="San Ángel">San Ángel</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHerrera2002179–180Zamora199046–47Burrus2005203_203-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHerrera2002179–180Zamora199046–47Burrus2005203-203">[201]</a></sup> Commissioned from <a href="/wiki/Le_Corbusier" title="Le Corbusier">Le Corbusier</a>'s student <a href="/wiki/Juan_O%27Gorman" title="Juan O'Gorman">Juan O'Gorman</a>, it consisted of two sections joined by a bridge; Kahlo's was painted blue and Rivera's pink and white.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHerrera2002179–180Zamora199046–47Kettenmann200338_204-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHerrera2002179–180Zamora199046–47Kettenmann200338-204">[202]</a></sup> The bohemian residence became an important meeting place for artists and political activists from Mexico and abroad.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBurrus2005203Herrera2002192–196_205-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBurrus2005203Herrera2002192–196-205">[203]</a></sup>
</p><p>Kahlo once again experienced health problems – undergoing an <a href="/wiki/Appendectomy" title="Appendectomy">appendectomy</a>, two abortions, and the amputation of <a href="/wiki/Gangrene" title="Gangrene">gangrenous</a> toes<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHerrera2002180–190Kettenmann200338–39Burrus2005219_206-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHerrera2002180–190Kettenmann200338–39Burrus2005219-206">[204]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Collins_152-1"><a href="#cite_note-Collins-152">[151]</a></sup> – and her marriage to Rivera had become strained. He was not happy to be back in Mexico and blamed Kahlo for their return.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHerrera2002180–182Zamora199046–47_207-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHerrera2002180–182Zamora199046–47-207">[205]</a></sup> While he had been unfaithful to her before, he now embarked on an affair with her younger sister <a href="/wiki/Cristina_Kahlo" title="Cristina Kahlo">Cristina</a>, which deeply hurt Kahlo's feelings.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHerrera2002180–182Zamora199046–47Burrus2005203Ankori2002159–160_208-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHerrera2002180–182Zamora199046–47Burrus2005203Ankori2002159–160-208">[206]</a></sup> After discovering the affair in early 1935, she moved to an apartment in central Mexico City and considered divorcing him.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBurrus2005203Herrera2002180–190Kettenmann200339_209-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBurrus2005203Herrera2002180–190Kettenmann200339-209">[207]</a></sup> She also had an affair of her own with American artist <a href="/wiki/Isamu_Noguchi" title="Isamu Noguchi">Isamu Noguchi</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHerrera2002180–190Kettenmann200338–40Zamora199050–53Burrus2005203Ankori2002193_210-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHerrera2002180–190Kettenmann200338–40Zamora199050–53Burrus2005203Ankori2002193-210">[208]</a></sup>
</p><p>Kahlo was reconciled with Rivera and Cristina later in 1935 and moved back to San Ángel.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBurrus2005203Herrera2002190–191Zamora199050_211-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBurrus2005203Herrera2002190–191Zamora199050-211">[209]</a></sup> She became a loving aunt to Cristina's children, Isolda and Antonio.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHerrera2002192–196_212-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHerrera2002192–196-212">[210]</a></sup> Despite the reconciliation, both Rivera and Kahlo continued their infidelities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHerrera2002192–201Zamora199050–53Kettenmann200340_213-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHerrera2002192–201Zamora199050–53Kettenmann200340-213">[211]</a></sup> She also resumed her political activities in 1936, joining the <a href="/wiki/Fourth_International" title="Fourth International">Fourth International</a> and becoming a founding member of a solidarity committee to provide aid to the <a href="/wiki/Second_Spanish_Republic" title="Second Spanish Republic">Republicans</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Civil_War" title="Spanish Civil War">Spanish Civil War</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKettenmann200340–41Burrus2005203_214-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKettenmann200340–41Burrus2005203-214">[212]</a></sup> She and Rivera successfully petitioned the Mexican government to grant asylum to former Soviet leader <a href="/wiki/Leon_Trotsky" title="Leon Trotsky">Leon Trotsky</a> and offered La Casa Azul for him and his wife <a href="/wiki/Natalia_Sedova" title="Natalia Sedova">Natalia Sedova</a> as a residence.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHerrera2002192–215Zamora199052–54Kettenmann200340–41Burrus2005203_215-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHerrera2002192–215Zamora199052–54Kettenmann200340–41Burrus2005203-215">[213]</a></sup> The couple lived there from January 1937 until April 1939, with Kahlo and Trotsky not only becoming good friends but also having a brief affair.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHerrera2002192–215Zamora199052–54Kettenmann200340–41_216-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHerrera2002192–215Zamora199052–54Kettenmann200340–41-216">[214]</a></sup>
</p>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1066479718" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><table class="infobox" style="float: right; clear: right; margin:0 0 1.5em 1.5em"><tbody><tr><th class="infobox-above" colspan="2" style="font-size:115%">External images</th></tr><tr><td class="infobox-full-data" colspan="2" style="text-align: left"><img alt="image icon" data-file-height="512" Nips</i> (1935)</a></td></tr><tr><td class="infobox-full-data" colspan="2" style="text-align: left"><img alt="image icon" data-file-height="512" data-file-width="512" decoding="async" height="16" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/6/61/Searchtool.svg/16px-Searchtool.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/6/61/Searchtool.svg/24px-Searchtool.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/6/61/Searchtool.svg/32px-Searchtool.svg.png 2x" width="16"/> <a class="external text" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/6/61/Searchtool.svg/16px-Searchtool.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/6/61/Searchtool.svg/24px-Searchtool.svg.png 1.5x,
